  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1c6c96b4-054d-4bb2-bf2c-ddfe88fd8723'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer5882606130962164929">Just about everything in Endora, Iowa (pop. 1,091 and dwindling) is eating Gilbert Grape, a twenty-four-year-old grocery clerk who dreams only of leaving.   <span id="freeText5882606130962164929" style="display:none">Just about everything in Endora, Iowa (pop. 1,091 and dwindling) is eating Gilbert Grape, a twenty-four-year-old grocery clerk who dreams only of leaving. His enormous mother, once the town sweetheart, has been eating nonstop ever since her husband's suicide, and the floor beneath her TV chair is threatening to cave in. Gilbert's long-suffering older sister, Amy, still mourns the death of Elvis, and his knockout younger sister has become hooked on makeup, boys, and Jesus--in that order, but the biggest event on the horizon for all the Grapes is the eighteenth birthday of Gilbert's younger brother, Arnie, who is a living miracle just for having survived so long. As the Grapes gather in Endora, a mysterious beauty glides through town on a bicycle and rides circles around Gilbert, until he begins to see a new vision of his family and himself.</span>

<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    They couldn't bury Momma without first using a crane to remove her from the house. This would have drawn a crowd and made Momma a fat-joke punchline. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    They couldn't bury Momma without first using a crane to remove her from the house. This would have drawn a crowd and made Momma a fat-joke punchline. Burning Momma gave her more dignity.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1822946480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9154224193005460181">What's Eating Gilbert Grape originally came out when I was in high school. As per my mother's rule, one had to read the book before viewing the movie so I read the story of the Grape family before venturing to watch the film starring Johnny Depp and Leonardo DiCaprio. Peter Hedges created many memorable characters in small town Endora, Iowa, also known derogatorily by Gilbert as Endora of the line. A touching story about a dysfunctional family wasting away as their mother Bonnie eats herself int</span>
  <span id="freeText9154224193005460181" style="display:none">What's Eating Gilbert Grape originally came out when I was in high school. As per my mother's rule, one had to read the book before viewing the movie so I read the story of the Grape family before venturing to watch the film starring Johnny Depp and Leonardo DiCaprio. Peter Hedges created many memorable characters in small town Endora, Iowa, also known derogatorily by Gilbert as Endora of the line. A touching story about a dysfunctional family wasting away as their mother Bonnie eats herself into oblivion, I rooted for Gilbert to get out of town the entire time. It has been twenty years since I read this charming novel, but Gilbert, Arnie, and Bonnie have stayed with me, and I recommend Peter Hedges' work to any looking for a book about small town America. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9154224193005460181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_965936737" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/965936737" />
    <a title="Idarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1283951-idarah"><img alt="Idarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596863879p2/1283951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/965936737?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Idarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Idarah" href="/user/show/1283951-idarah">Idarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283951-idarah?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer965936737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14227811186082738554"><blockquote>
  <b>“You can tell the idyllic nature of a family by the upkeep of its picnic table. Ours is its own indictment. We are splintering and peeling. We rot.” – Gilbert Grape</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Before Jonathan Safran Foer was the talk of literary circles for writing <i>Everything is Illuminated</i> at such a young age, there was Peter Hedges. <i>What's Eating Gilbert Grape</i> is his profound post-coming-of-age novel about twenty-four year old Gilbert Grape, a grocery store stock boy living in the tiny town of Endora, Iowa. Grappling </span>
  <span id="freeText14227811186082738554" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>“You can tell the idyllic nature of a family by the upkeep of its picnic table. Ours is its own indictment. We are splintering and peeling. We rot.” – Gilbert Grape</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Before Jonathan Safran Foer was the talk of literary circles for writing <i>Everything is Illuminated</i> at such a young age, there was Peter Hedges. <i>What's Eating Gilbert Grape</i> is his profound post-coming-of-age novel about twenty-four year old Gilbert Grape, a grocery store stock boy living in the tiny town of Endora, Iowa. Grappling with the desire to leave town and start an exciting life elsewhere, and the guilt and responsibility to stay and care for his family, he is unprepared when a beautiful young girl from the big city comes to town, and unexpectedly helps him come to terms with his feelings about his family and their past.<br /><br />Considering how old Hedges was when he wrote this, it too was equally profound. Being a fan of the movie though, the book was definitely more gratifying. Gilbert is a complex young man, and several times I found myself thinking about how Johnny Depp was the perfect actor for this character. I was also struck by the loving relationship Gilbert has with his disabled brother, Arnie, probably one of the most astute characters in the book. I am so glad I found this book (for one dollar, no less). It seemed to be the perfect time to read it and reflect on the different crossroads we come to at various stages in our life, and the thoughts that pervade our mind in an attempt to ensure that we're making the best decision possible.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14227811186082738554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_380666366" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/380666366" />
    <a title="Caroline " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3236194-caroline"><img alt="Caroline " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576541068p2/3236194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/380666366?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline " href="/user/show/3236194-caroline">Caroline </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3236194-caroline?shelf=he-wrote-it">he-wrote-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3236194-caroline?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3236194-caroline?shelf=family-drama">family-drama</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer380666366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14213262087352376598">***NO SPOILERS***<br/><br/>What’s eating Gilbert Grape? In short, a lot:<br/><br/>-His general ennui and restlessness in tiny, dead-end Endora, Iowa<br/>-His morbidly obese mother<br/>-His intellectually handicapped brother<br/>-His romantic relationship<br/><br/>This is not all. Further topics Peter Hedges wrote about are as follows:<br/><br/>-Economic depression<br/>-Adultery<br/>-Sudden death<br/>-Family shame<br/>-Suicide<br/><br/>It’s too much, and it’s the book’s biggest flaw. Nevertheless, Hedges didn’t explore these to an equal degree. Endora is just wallpaper. The adult</span>
  <span id="freeText14213262087352376598" style="display:none">***NO SPOILERS***<br /><br />What’s eating Gilbert Grape? In short, a lot:<br /><br />-His general ennui and restlessness in tiny, dead-end Endora, Iowa<br />-His morbidly obese mother<br />-His intellectually handicapped brother<br />-His romantic relationship<br /><br />This is not all. Further topics Peter Hedges wrote about are as follows:<br /><br />-Economic depression<br />-Adultery<br />-Sudden death<br />-Family shame<br />-Suicide<br /><br />It’s too much, and it’s the book’s biggest flaw. Nevertheless, Hedges didn’t explore these to an equal degree. Endora is just wallpaper. The adultery is randomly tossed in, as is a sudden death and Gilbert’s romance. The economic depression is disappointingly undeveloped. Hedges wanted to stuff it all into one book, but he couldn’t; that would've meant a book 1,000 pages long. <br /><br />Hedges’s most promising story lines involve Gilbert’s obese mother, Bonnie, and intellectually handicapped brother, Arnie. I was therefore most disappointed that he didn’t develop these characters, especially Bonnie, as well as he could. <br /><br />She’s reduced to a sleeping, eating, demanding lump, a passive figure who I learned about more via narration from Gilbert rather than via direct characterization. There’s only brief backstory, but what’s clear is that there’s a lot eating <i>her</i>, and that has a great deal of relevance to what’s eating Gilbert. Gilbert resents what a burden she is, but that’s only ever apparent because of his references to her as a “whale” or “walrus.” The story demands she be more developed. <br /><br />Along the same lines, Arnie comes across as little more than a mischievous sprite who enjoys climbing Endora’s water tower and is always in need of a good scrubbing. Intellectually handicapped characters beg for multi-dimensional depictions (think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36576608.Flowers_for_Algernon" title="Flowers for Algernon by Daniel Keyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Flowers for Algernon</a>). The story demands more…<i>everything</i> about him. <br /><br />Of everyone in the Grape family, Bonnie and Arnie are the most intriguing, but what’s most important is they’re the ones trapping Gilbert in Endora. At one point, Hedges provided a glimpse into what could have been, and the story turns brilliant--it goes to that exact deeper, sobering place it needs to go--but just as quickly he reverted to the superficial: having Gilbert simply complain about his mom and to the usual goofy portrayal of Arnie. <br /><br /><i>What’s Eating Gilbert Grape</i> could have been really something if it had Gilbert and Bonnie just as they are, but with a honed mother-and-son focus or if it had Gilbert and Arnie just as they are, but with the honed focus on him and his brother. Or, if Hedges wanted to be ambitious, it could have all three, fully developed. <br /><br />Hedges may have failed with Arnie and Bonnie, but some of his other characters are stronger and have their place. These are Gilbert’s older sister Amy as the caretaker and provider, his vain teenage sister Ellen, his always-cheerful boss, and his best friend. They make the book worth reading. The romantic interest, Becky, however, is a notable exception. <br /><br />His relationship with Becky is one of the things eating Gilbert, yet it’s not for the reason it should be: the fact that he’s a 24-year-old man fantasizing about and romancing a 15-year-old girl. Becky is a sage who speaks so maturely that I thought she was an adult before Hedges revealed that she’s just a teen. This may have been purposeful on Hedges’s part, to distract from the reality. But since this side plot isn't about Gilbert’s grappling with his conscience, Hedges could have made Becky Gilbert’s age without hurting anything in this section. Her many wise statements--which sound ridiculous coming from a 15-year-old--would also then square with her age. <br /><br />I did really enjoy this book for most of the characters. I was invested in learning about these small-town residents and about Endora. I didn’t get the latter wish, but I got enough of the former to keep me reading. <br /><br />Most of all, I was curious about what was eating Gilbert Grape--but I’m still not sure about this. Too much in this story is scattered, some is a rough sketch, and some is entirely irrelevant. As a result, <i>What’s Eating Gilbert Grape</i> is more of a light read, and that’s a shame, because I doubt that’s what Peter Hedges intended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14213262087352376598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1119390786" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1119390786" />
    <a title="Kandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice"><img alt="Kandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231810788p2/1396160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1119390786?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kandice" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice">Kandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1396160-kandice?shelf=1412-challenge">1412-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1119390786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3582648073325368001">Gilbert Grape lives at home with two of his three sisters, Amy and Ellen, and one of his two brothers, Arnie. Arnie is mentally handicapped and depends on Gilbert for a lot. So do his sisters, but Arnie's dependence is draining. Then there's Gilbert's momma. She also lives with them and is <b>poifectly huge</b>. Like hundreds of pounds worth of huge. She was once the prettiest girl in Endora where the Grape family home is located, but now...is not. The whole Grape clan is just counting the days to Arni</span>
  <span id="freeText3582648073325368001" style="display:none">Gilbert Grape lives at home with two of his three sisters, Amy and Ellen, and one of his two brothers, Arnie. Arnie is mentally handicapped and depends on Gilbert for a lot. So do his sisters, but Arnie's dependence is draining. Then there's Gilbert's momma. She also lives with them and is <b>poifectly huge</b>. Like hundreds of pounds worth of huge. She was once the prettiest girl in Endora where the Grape family home is located, but now...is not. The whole Grape clan is just counting the days to Arnie's 18th birthday. The birthday the doctors said he would never see. <br /><br />Poor Gilbert works so hard to keep his family afloat. He's 24 and simply cannot live his own life. His family needs him, his mental support and, yes, his paycheck, to survive. Gilbert's dad, Mr. Grape, has been dead for 17 years and with his older brother gone everything falls on Gilbert's shoulders. There's never any time for Gilbert. A few stolen moments here or there, but even they are tinged in guilt and regret.<br /><br />This book was lovely. Not because it was sweet, or because I loved Gilbert, he could be quite the shit, but I defy anyone to live under the circumstances and burdens Gilbert endured every day and not be one at least occasionally. It was lovely because it was realistic. There are no Mother Theresa's among us today. There are just people doing what they can to get by. Doing what has to be done to get their family and loved ones one day closer to happiness. Yes, Gilbert lost patience with Arnie and his sisters on occasion, but he still stayed and cared for his family in the best way he knew how. In a very sad, but real way.<br /><br />The Grape clan was a bunch of characters to say the least and Gilbert's friends and fellow citizens were every bit as quirky, but anyone who has ever lived in a small town knows this is the way people really are. It's the normal people who get out. It's the regular people who leave town to find their dreams and futures. It's as if the real characters are a little larger than the Regular Joes so are caught in the sieve of small town life. Too big to fall through the screen, but small enough to feel the pinch.<br /><br />This book touches on the loss of small town life with the Mom n Pop establishments. The encroachment of Wal-Marts and Krogers on sweet ol' Main Street USA. It shows us that not only the old codgers mourn the loss, but some of the younger generation as well. Gilbert's romance with the new to town Becky is just one more example of the uniqueness of small town folk. Becky belonged in Endora in the same way Gilbert belongs and for some of the same reasons that Gilbert's older siblings who have left town do not. Small town life takes a certain fortitude and strength. Gilbert has it. Becky may as well. The Grape kids who have left do not.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3582648073325368001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_10195099" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10195099" />
    <a title="Madeline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111921-madeline"><img alt="Madeline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1220803522p2/111921.jpg" /></a>

  <span id="freeText2503485560891951149" style="display:none">One of the few books where I enjoyed the movie version more. Here are some unsettling things about the book version that got left out of the movie:<br />-Gilbert is kind of an asshole, especially the way he constantly refers to his brother as "the retard."     <a title="Matt  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/909857-matt"><img alt="Matt  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203470644p2/909857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152273300?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt  " href="/user/show/909857-matt">Matt  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671870805" href="/book/show/1067938.What_s_Eating_Gilbert_Grape">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152273300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16755905736731279451">From a passage in the book where Momma is talking to Gilbert about motherhood/creastion: "I see you and I know that I'm a god. Or a goddess. Godlike! And this house is my kingdom. Yes, Gilbert. This chair is my throne. And you, Gilbert, are my knight in shimmering armor."..."Shining, I think, Momma, is what you mean."..."No, I know what I mean. You don't shine, Gilbert. You shimmer. You hear?. You shimmer!"<br/><br/>My dictionary defines shimmer as a verb and as a noun: to shine with or reflect a soft, tr</span>
  <span id="freeText16755905736731279451" style="display:none">From a passage in the book where Momma is talking to Gilbert about motherhood/creastion: "I see you and I know that I'm a god. Or a goddess. Godlike! And this house is my kingdom. Yes, Gilbert. This chair is my throne. And you, Gilbert, are my knight in shimmering armor."..."Shining, I think, Momma, is what you mean."..."No, I know what I mean. You don't shine, Gilbert. You shimmer. You hear?. You shimmer!"<br /><br />My dictionary defines shimmer as a verb and as a noun: to shine with or reflect a soft, tremulous light; a soft tremulous light. <br /><br />This novel shimmers with that soft, tremulous light. It is a subtle story, written in a subtle style. One is surprised to find what appear to be nondescript sentences that are actually keys to the book, great with meaning. The above discussion of "shimmer" is such an example. As is this, possibly my favorite sentence in the book, marking the moment of Gilbert's, for lack of a better word, awakening: "And as the remaining dirt on Arnie starts washing away, it begins." <br />I have wanted to read this book for years. And now I have. And it was worth the wait. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16755905736731279451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14406409858071804604">You know what makes me hang my head in shame?<br/>The fact that I didn't know this book was a book until earlier this year.<br/>I am not even kidding. Yes, I am a librarian and have been for a really long time and still, I had no idea this was a book.<br/>So much shame for me.<br/>My ridiculous excuse that I just now made up to make myself feel better about my prior ignorance: This came out in 1991 and I had been in college for a year and was getting the hang of things and really buckling down to study and such. I </span>
  <span id="freeText14406409858071804604" style="display:none">You know what makes me hang my head in shame?<br />The fact that I didn't know this book was a book until earlier this year.<br />I am not even kidding. Yes, I am a librarian and have been for a really long time and still, I had no idea this was a book.<br />So much shame for me.<br />My ridiculous excuse that I just now made up to make myself feel better about my prior ignorance: This came out in 1991 and I had been in college for a year and was getting the hang of things and really buckling down to study and such. I didn't read for pleasure anymore and I think all fiction that came out between 1990-1995 that didn't go through the library was missed by me. That's my excuse.<br />Anyway, I now know this is a book and I have read it.<br /><br />It makes the movie make a lot more sense. I liked the movie quite well (I did see that when it came out; I also just watched it the other night for the sake of comparison and if it said "Based on the book by Peter Hedges" in the beginning, I missed it both the first time and when I watched it again on Friday) but I like the book a lot better. It's much more nuanced, the relationships between everyone are deeper, more real, more painful. I could relate with Book Gilbert far better than I could with Movie Gilbert and now I don't think Juliette Lewis was such a good choice.<br />But whatever.<br />This was a solid story and the ending is much more powerful in text, at least it was for me.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_144152182" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144152182" />
    <a title="Vanessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/752176-vanessa"><img alt="Vanessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199757927p2/752176.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144152182?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa" href="/user/show/752176-vanessa">Vanessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144152182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15524552526369754272">I have this friend who has a rule (although he will deny that it's a rule) that he won't see movies if he has read the book-and vice versa-because it's a waste of time when there are so many movies to be seen and books to be read. And sometimes that is true but I am pretty much the opposite. If I liked the book, I'm curious to see how they adapt it for the screen. If I liked the movie or at least found it interesting, I want to go back to read the book to fill in the inevitable blanks. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/359770.House_of_Sand_and_Fog' title='House of Sand and Fog by Andre Dubus III' rel='nofollow noopener'>House of </a></span>
  <span id="freeText15524552526369754272" style="display:none">I have this friend who has a rule (although he will deny that it's a rule) that he won't see movies if he has read the book-and vice versa-because it's a waste of time when there are so many movies to be seen and books to be read. And sometimes that is true but I am pretty much the opposite. If I liked the book, I'm curious to see how they adapt it for the screen. If I liked the movie or at least found it interesting, I want to go back to read the book to fill in the inevitable blanks. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/359770.House_of_Sand_and_Fog" title="House of Sand and Fog by Andre Dubus III" rel="nofollow noopener">House of Sand and Fog</a>, for example, was a great adaptation of the book but ended when there was still half the book to go. Ditto for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68797.Cavedweller" title="Cavedweller by Dorothy Allison" rel="nofollow noopener">Cavedweller</a>.<br /><br />Then you've got a book like this, which takes the same characters (Gilbert Grape and his dysfunctional family remnants) and setting (a dying small town in rural Iowa) but has a totally different mood from the film. Which is interesting since Hedges wrote both the book and the screenplay. As cliche as it is to drag out Salinger's ghost, Gilbert Grape, age 24, has a distinct Holden Caulfield-ish aura about him. Call him "Catcher in the Soybeans." He works stocking shelves at a local grocery that is barely surviving since a chain store opened nearby. He and his older sister care for their teenage sister, his mentally challenged brother and their mother who has pretty much been eating her grief since their father hung himself almost 20 years ago in their basement. She has become so large that she is virtually immobile, hasn't left the house in years, and the floor beneath her chair is now starting to cave in. It sounds unbearably maudlin perhaps at this point. Thanks to the misanthropic yet likable narrator, it's not. <br /><br />I don't know how to describe this book. Parts were sad, parts were very funny. I didn't totally click with it for some reason. Perhaps it's because I'm a heathen who never totally appreciated Salinger? But I can understand how other people can love it. <br /><br />The movie, on the other hand, is one of my all-time favorites.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15524552526369754272" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23812025-what-s-eating-gilbert-grape">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39109173-karolina-kat?shelf=adapted">adapted</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1255344398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12982587598593508300"><i>You don’t shine, Gilbert. You shimmer. You hear? You shimmer!</i><br/><br/>Like many before me, for a long time I had no idea that there was a book upon which one of the most important movies of my adolescent years was based. <br/>The story of the Grape family in the novel is more realistic, while all the characters are simply more human. There aren't that many good people in the little town of Endora, and Gilbert falls rightin between the white and the black.<br/><br/><i>[...]there’s nothing worse than being told you’re good </i></span>
  <span id="freeText12982587598593508300" style="display:none"><i>You don’t shine, Gilbert. You shimmer. You hear? You shimmer!</i><br /><br />Like many before me, for a long time I had no idea that there was a book upon which one of the most important movies of my adolescent years was based. <br />The story of the Grape family in the novel is more realistic, while all the characters are simply more human. There aren't that many good people in the little town of Endora, and Gilbert falls rightin between the white and the black.<br /><br /><i>[...]there’s nothing worse than being told you’re good when you know you’re bad.</i><br /><br />Gilbert from the novel is more overwhelmed with life, his perception of people surrounding him sharper, and having him as the narrator/focalizer makes for a very drastic point of view. <br />Surprisingly it is the book, not movie, that brings the flesh and bone to Gilbert's struggles and to people around him, who do not serve as background characters but simply feel as other real people living in Endora.<br /><br />Arnie's illness is far less pretty, Amy's struggles are far harder, and his mother is more disturbed than in the movie. And there is far more that's eating Gilbert Grape.<br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1169858517" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1169858517" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1169858517?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780671735098" href="/book/show/1159608.What_s_Eating_Gilbert_Grape">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1169858517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5893784337763309578">If you haven't read this book or seen the film adaptation, this is one book you should definitely read at some point because it's an amazingly written coming-of-age story about a young man dealing with a dysfunctional family while trying to find his own place in the world as well. His mom is seen by the townspeople as being a gross, lazy pig, but Gilbert often is saddened to think that at one time she was considered extremely beautiful - and to him and his broken yet closely-knit family, she sti</span>
  <span id="freeText5893784337763309578" style="display:none">If you haven't read this book or seen the film adaptation, this is one book you should definitely read at some point because it's an amazingly written coming-of-age story about a young man dealing with a dysfunctional family while trying to find his own place in the world as well. His mom is seen by the townspeople as being a gross, lazy pig, but Gilbert often is saddened to think that at one time she was considered extremely beautiful - and to him and his broken yet closely-knit family, she still is. His brother, Arnie, is "retarded" as Gilbert puts it - but Gilbert cares very much for him and tries his best to keep the town gawkers, gossips and bullies away. The small town Gilbert lives in is facing economical changes and Gilbert himself is having issues with women. Somewhere in all this tangled mess comes a brilliant and inspiring story of love in the most troubling times, and unforgettable characters, an original plot and a lot of nostalgia.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5893784337763309578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Karin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20048682-karin"><img alt="Karin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588016778p2/20048682.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3282988613?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karin" href="/user/show/20048682-karin">Karin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=american">american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=play-book-tag">play-book-tag</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=american-authors">american-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=iowa">iowa</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=dysfunctional-families">dysfunctional-families</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=american-author">american-author</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3282988613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2736049762805682606">This book was written fairly well, which is why it's two stars and not one.<br/><br/>This book does have humour in it, but it's not a happy book. Gilbert Grape is part of a highly dysfunctional family still suffering in their own ways since his dad was found in the basement after hanging himself, and in addition, his younger brother Arnie has special needs. They are dysfunctional because none of them has had any sort of help in handling their feelings and issues since then. <br/><br/>If you like really psychologica</span>
  <span id="freeText2736049762805682606" style="display:none">This book was written fairly well, which is why it's two stars and not one.<br /><br />This book does have humour in it, but it's not a happy book. Gilbert Grape is part of a highly dysfunctional family still suffering in their own ways since his dad was found in the basement after hanging himself, and in addition, his younger brother Arnie has special needs. They are dysfunctional because none of them has had any sort of help in handling their feelings and issues since then. <br /><br />If you like really psychological, darkly funny novels about families in crisis, then you may well like this book. There is a redeeming feature to this book--a very redeeming feature, but that goes beyond the kinds of things I include in my review.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12275620291137425527">One of my very favorite books. I'd seen (and loved) the movie version before picking up this book, but it was the style of writing that made it jump out to me and establish itself as separate. Gilbert's inner monologue? Brilliant and hilarious, I could go on and on. It felt so REAL to me. Mr. Hedges is very talented. Through the prose I was enveloped in the sleepy town vibe so completely that I felt as if Endora were my own hometown, familiar in every way. I continue to recommend this book to an</span>
  <span id="freeText12275620291137425527" style="display:none">One of my very favorite books. I'd seen (and loved) the movie version before picking up this book, but it was the style of writing that made it jump out to me and establish itself as separate. Gilbert's inner monologue? Brilliant and hilarious, I could go on and on. It felt so REAL to me. Mr. Hedges is very talented. Through the prose I was enveloped in the sleepy town vibe so completely that I felt as if Endora were my own hometown, familiar in every way. I continue to recommend this book to anyone searching for a good read, and no one has been disappointed so far.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2673503975?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ginger Bensman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ginger Bensman" href="/user/show/8783847-ginger-bensman">Ginger Bensman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8783847-ginger-bensman?shelf=general-fiction">general-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2673503975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9758819046694807300">Gilbert (smart, handsome, horny, and twenty-four) is stuck in small town rural America and going nowhere. The operative word here is “stuck”. He is tethered (duty bound) to a despondent and tragically widowed mother (Bonnie Grape) who is morbidly obese, eats junk food by the pallet, and smokes up a storm while she watches television in her upstairs room where the floor beneath her bulges perilously. Bonnie’s one desperate wish is to see Gilbert’s younger, developmentally delayed brother, Arnie (</span>
  <span id="freeText9758819046694807300" style="display:none">Gilbert (smart, handsome, horny, and twenty-four) is stuck in small town rural America and going nowhere. The operative word here is “stuck”. He is tethered (duty bound) to a despondent and tragically widowed mother (Bonnie Grape) who is morbidly obese, eats junk food by the pallet, and smokes up a storm while she watches television in her upstairs room where the floor beneath her bulges perilously. Bonnie’s one desperate wish is to see Gilbert’s younger, developmentally delayed brother, Arnie (who wasn’t supposed to survive much past infancy), turn 18. And so we embark on Arnie’s big year. Gilbert, his sisters (Amy, Ellen and Janice) and his older brother, Larry, have (each in their own way) been primed and are struggling toward Arnie’s special day. Walk a mile, or two, or three, in Gilbert’s shoes. The trek is sad, snarky, darkly funny and largely engaging (if overlong at times to the point of being a bit tedious). </span>
  <a data-text-id="9758819046694807300" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Mad Dog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2844089-mad-dog"><img alt="Mad Dog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1287532944p2/2844089.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mad Dog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mad Dog" href="/user/show/2844089-mad-dog">Mad Dog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2844089-mad-dog?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143783662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4719543031182116909">This book is not really informative, deep, or insightful. I am talking about the first person narrator (Gilbert) as well as the book. Gilbert is thoroughly mediocre in thought and deed. He wears a 'perma-frown'. He likes to brood. The book relies on his thoughts more than his actions, as he is very passive(repressed). Most of the supporting characters are annoyingly shallow. <br/><br/>None of this really sounds like a good book to me.<br/><br/>But this book (and Gilbert) did very much captivate me. I am rooting har</span>
  <span id="freeText4719543031182116909" style="display:none">This book is not really informative, deep, or insightful. I am talking about the first person narrator (Gilbert) as well as the book. Gilbert is thoroughly mediocre in thought and deed. He wears a 'perma-frown'. He likes to brood. The book relies on his thoughts more than his actions, as he is very passive(repressed). Most of the supporting characters are annoyingly shallow. <br /><br />None of this really sounds like a good book to me.<br /><br />But this book (and Gilbert) did very much captivate me. I am rooting hard for Gilbert, a guy that I would probably dislike in 'real life'. What propels me through this book is affection and hope. Gilbert is affecting because he simply recognizes what is good and true. He is sensitve to what is good and true. Gilbert is affecting because he is sad and I want him to be happy. I want him to be able to 'live out' what is 'good and true'. But he is not graceful when confronted with the foolishness of others. And he doesn't say enough (or do enough) when confronted with the 'good and true' that he desires. He broods about events in the past and 'things' that are out of his control. So there are multiple obstacles. This is the suspense of the book.<br /><br />Go Gilbert!! <br /><br /><i>One brain teaser for me (about this book) is this: What would this book be like if Gilbert is not handsome? Gilbert has a certain aura that draws people to him. The community (in this book) seems to have a rooting interest in Gilbert. This probably would be removed if Gilbert is not handsome, and the book would be much different.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4719543031182116909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91042626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15091074074927819655"> I loved this book! The story is simple but engaging and the character of Gilbert Grape is one of the most well constructed male characters I’ve read in a long time. I enjoyed it so much because it’s not quite a coming of age story; Gilbert is older and feels the adult pressures of being a grown up but he’s still young enough that his life has not passed him by, even though he thinks it has, and all these other characters in the book are trying to show him this. <br/> Coming from a “unique” family my</span>
  <span id="freeText15091074074927819655" style="display:none"> I loved this book! The story is simple but engaging and the character of Gilbert Grape is one of the most well constructed male characters I’ve read in a long time. I enjoyed it so much because it’s not quite a coming of age story; Gilbert is older and feels the adult pressures of being a grown up but he’s still young enough that his life has not passed him by, even though he thinks it has, and all these other characters in the book are trying to show him this. <br /> Coming from a “unique” family myself, this story endures itself to me as much for the good of it’s characters but also their flaws. My only regret is that I wish I had read this book sooner!<br /> Excellent writing, excellent characters and an amazing story…what else can you ask for in a book?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15091074074927819655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1430062067?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DJ" href="/user/show/3947281-dj">DJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947281-dj?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947281-dj?shelf=motion-picture-adapted">motion-picture-adapted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947281-dj?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1430062067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8856204308062190125">This is a tough one for me to rate. I mean, I read it forever and a day ago, but forgot some of the parts. Have seen the movie a million and a half times, and still adore it to this day. <br/><br/>But for me, the book felt like it was missing some pieces. Not that it has to do with that "show-not-tell" stuff everyone is cramming down everyone's throats in books these days. I like a skimmed down, show the important things to the main character, get to the story way this book is told. It doesn't play around</span>
  <span id="freeText8856204308062190125" style="display:none">This is a tough one for me to rate. I mean, I read it forever and a day ago, but forgot some of the parts. Have seen the movie a million and a half times, and still adore it to this day. <br /><br />But for me, the book felt like it was missing some pieces. Not that it has to do with that "show-not-tell" stuff everyone is cramming down everyone's throats in books these days. I like a skimmed down, show the important things to the main character, get to the story way this book is told. It doesn't play around and take a hundred words to make a point.<br /><br />The book does, however, use the word "retard" a lot. A LOT!!! Of course, it was written before PC became the norm. And you forget how things used to be until you read the older books. But this wasn't also what took off some stars for me.<br /><br />I think it was because in the book, Gilbert and Becky weren't the same from what I LOVE about the movie. She's lackadaisical and he's uptight and stressed. Here, Becky was more annoying little girl than chase the world. Gilbert was ultra stressed out, but sometimes, I thought he was going to be POSTAL over some of the instances. Reading him stressed me out.<br /><br />Another thing was the additional siblings of the Grape family. I didn't like Larry, nor could I see him belonging. (And maybe that's how he's supposed to be.) Then Janice...WTH? I didn't like her either. Again, she didn't belong, and I'm not sure how intentional it was to have her feel that way.<br /><br />The story is still good. My favorite parts of the movie were in here...<br /><br />But the largest killer of the story was the ending. Nothing like the book. Nothing to make me feel Gilbert is finally living his OWN LIFE whether he would stay in Endora or leave. I just wanted that somewhat happy resolution for this tortured character who NEVER SEEMED to get a win. <br /><br />I've got to find that movie and watch it, fix where the book fell flat for me.<br /><br />*RANDOM READ - because you can't read a paper book in the dark. Thank Heavens for Kindle!* </span>
  <a data-text-id="8856204308062190125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_152003206" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152003206" />
    <a title="Marialyce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1277371-marialyce"><img alt="Marialyce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601165932p2/1277371.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152003206?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marialyce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marialyce" href="/user/show/1277371-marialyce">Marialyce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1277371-marialyce?shelf=2011-group-reads">2011-group-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1277371-marialyce?shelf=march-2011">march-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152003206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11999856744061516017">Another title for this book could have been "Dysfunctional Family Personified." While I did enjoy the read, I felt that the subject matter has been done often and frankly a lot better. We follow Gilbert and his family of siblings and a grossly overweight mother through their sufferings and eventually experience their love realizations of each other. Sorrow and pity abound for this family as we witness the destruction of this unit which seemed to be kicked off by the suicide of the father. The si</span>
  <span id="freeText11999856744061516017" style="display:none">Another title for this book could have been "Dysfunctional Family Personified." While I did enjoy the read, I felt that the subject matter has been done often and frankly a lot better. We follow Gilbert and his family of siblings and a grossly overweight mother through their sufferings and eventually experience their love realizations of each other. Sorrow and pity abound for this family as we witness the destruction of this unit which seemed to be kicked off by the suicide of the father. The siblings are very cognizant of their situation while Gilbert seems to be the most effected by the desperation of being "the man" in the family. Saddled with a "retard" (his words not mine) for his younger brother, he tries to reconcile his existence and place the family in a somewhat order.( or was it disorder?)<br /><br />It seems what Mr Hedges is trying to say is that no matter how bad your family may be, they still love you so that makes all well, doesn't it? I suppose for the time in which it was written, that this book was intended to shake up readers to the realization that a) don't think your family is the worst, and b) someone always has things worse than you do. We were suppose to feel sorry for Gilbert and all of the others. I felt the author seemed more engaged in trying to shock the reader than present a sympathetic view of this group of misfits. <br /><br />I read this book quickly and though the topic was serious and sad. Sorry to say that I just could not give a topic such as this one read, the deep I thought that it deserved. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11999856744061516017" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer692372603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10331080874104117296">I really enjoyed this book. <br/><br/>There is a sensibility to Hedges' writing I found endearing and addictive. Yes, the dialogue is sometimes a little forced and some of the characters are a tad too eccentric to come off real, but Gilbert Grape's voice makes up for all of that.<br/><br/>This is a great novel I'm glad I finally read.<br/><br/>I almost feel like I lived in Endora for the last two days. For anyone who's grown up in a small town, this tale will resonate with you. <br/><br/>Gilbert's resistance to Food Land and Burger Ba</span>
  <span id="freeText10331080874104117296" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book. <br /><br />There is a sensibility to Hedges' writing I found endearing and addictive. Yes, the dialogue is sometimes a little forced and some of the characters are a tad too eccentric to come off real, but Gilbert Grape's voice makes up for all of that.<br /><br />This is a great novel I'm glad I finally read.<br /><br />I almost feel like I lived in Endora for the last two days. For anyone who's grown up in a small town, this tale will resonate with you. <br /><br />Gilbert's resistance to Food Land and Burger Barns, is noble but futile.<br /><br />Peter Hedges does such a wonderful job at capturing the hate we can have for our family, while loving them with a vengeance. There is something about this story that really spoke to me. <br /><br />I can't quite put my finger on it. <br /><br />And maybe that's the magic of it. This sort of feeling like you know all these people: Larry the brother who won't deal but will succeed. Janice the sister who could have been great, but turned into an underachiever, Ellen, the sister who was given the looks, but little self-esteem, Arnie, the baby, the challenged, the one who knows that the emperor has no clothes. And finally, Gilbert, the family member who seems to know the truth about everybody else, yet, won't see his own.<br /><br />We know these people. We are these people. <br /><br />I think this was Hedges first novel and I think he loved these characters fiercely, and it comes through, right down to the last luminous and necessary word.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10331080874104117296" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_379969950" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/379969950" />
    <a title="Brian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/160726-brian"><img alt="Brian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1234625873p2/160726.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/379969950?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian" href="/user/show/160726-brian">Brian</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer379969950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17654818351824570620"><i>What’s Eating Gilbert Grape?</i> from the perspective of someone who grew up in Iowa -- that field-of-dreams, first-to-the-primaries, nothing-but-corn-and-more-corn mythical paradise that purports to be the heartbeat of the United States -- is a romance. Romance, not in sense of 24 year old Gilbert being torn between an affair with a married woman old enough to be his mum and a femme fatal 15 year old from Michigan, but in the sense of Don Quixote in quest of the Holy Grail, of Holden Caulfield sear</span>
  <span id="freeText17654818351824570620" style="display:none"><i>What’s Eating Gilbert Grape?</i> from the perspective of someone who grew up in Iowa -- that field-of-dreams, first-to-the-primaries, nothing-but-corn-and-more-corn mythical paradise that purports to be the heartbeat of the United States -- is a romance. Romance, not in sense of 24 year old Gilbert being torn between an affair with a married woman old enough to be his mum and a femme fatal 15 year old from Michigan, but in the sense of Don Quixote in quest of the Holy Grail, of Holden Caulfield searching for honesty. Gilbert is looking for a path around his family in a state where family is a synonym for the deity. He is searching for a way to hang onto a past that has already become the future. He is an angry young man, as likeable as most mythical Iowans are raised to become. Hedges wastes little breath dancing around the loveliness of small town folk and Midwest sunsets. Nor does he elevate Gilbert’s quest to the level of Indiana Jones in terms of pace or action. <i>Grape</i> is sometimes amusing, sometimes poignant, but right to the highly choreographed conclusion, it is an adventure. Without the pretence of a suit of armour, Gilbert tackles one everyday dragon after another until he finally confronts himself in the mirror.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17654818351824570620" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_62023579" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62023579" />
    <a title="Lesley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2483427-lesley"><img alt="Lesley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1246688441p2/2483427.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62023579?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lesley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lesley" href="/user/show/2483427-lesley">Lesley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2483427-lesley?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62023579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer739823365157416075">This is by far one of my favorite books! Before reading this novel, I had previously read Hedges's other novel, <u>An Ocean in Iowa</u>. Both are fantastic! Those of you avoiding the novel because you've seen the movie are making a mistake. Gilbert is an amazing character who struggles to understand his role in the world. His musings are both funny and introspective and make you think of a time when you felt the same ennui with life. I've followed Hedges's career since, and though he doesn't write nove</span>
  <span id="freeText739823365157416075" style="display:none">This is by far one of my favorite books! Before reading this novel, I had previously read Hedges's other novel, <u>An Ocean in Iowa</u>. Both are fantastic! Those of you avoiding the novel because you've seen the movie are making a mistake. Gilbert is an amazing character who struggles to understand his role in the world. His musings are both funny and introspective and make you think of a time when you felt the same ennui with life. I've followed Hedges's career since, and though he doesn't write novels anymore, his film career has filled the void. He still manages to display the same tenderness, and heartbreaking solitude within each of his characters. I highly recommend this read!!</span>

<div id="review_591170488" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/591170488" />
    <a title="J.T. Holden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5529137-j-t-holden"><img alt="J.T. Holden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481995490p2/5529137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/591170488?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.T. Holden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.T. Holden" href="/user/show/5529137-j-t-holden">J.T. Holden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer591170488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1375777966177676646">Hedges' masterful first novel should be studied and studied (and studied again) by anyone thinking of writing a book in the first-person/present-tense because it is a style that only lends itself properly to a particular voice, rhythm, and cadence. It should never be approached in the same manner as a novel written in the more common first-person/<i>past</i>-tense. That said, <i>What's Eating Gilbert Grape</i> is nothing short of a modern classic. I've read it over 30 times (on one particular occasion, I imme</span>
  <span id="freeText1375777966177676646" style="display:none">Hedges' masterful first novel should be studied and studied (and studied again) by anyone thinking of writing a book in the first-person/present-tense because it is a style that only lends itself properly to a particular voice, rhythm, and cadence. It should never be approached in the same manner as a novel written in the more common first-person/<i>past</i>-tense. That said, <i>What's Eating Gilbert Grape</i> is nothing short of a modern classic. I've read it over 30 times (on one particular occasion, I immediately turned to the first page after finishing the last and started reading again), and I know with complete certainty that I will read it many more times before my time is done. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1375777966177676646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hEfFh29hhgfQvEZXazRKDVkzt6cQ+hUwrg8SIBQyI9AaRIq2lIWGW7lA3vBGCs10KNjkJPKytgMpis9QN1Su2Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('17AlCOoV8XMMCeIOwzWS2wp+863A9JQuU17BaOQ1MxFJs2o5EfHxL2X1eqnuCxWie5WgLiK8Nx3U2xwYx1O+GA==')})
  }

Motivated by the promise he made to himself as a fatherless child to never abandon his own children, the two spent almost a year moving among shelters, &quot;HO-tels,&quot; soup lines, and even sleeping in the public restroom of a subway station.\n\nNever giving in to despair, Gardner made an astonishing transformation from being part of the city\'s invisible poor to being a powerful player in its financial district.\n\nMore than a memoir of Gardner\'s financial success, this is the story of a man who breaks his own family\'s cycle of men abandoning their children. <span id="freeTextContainer8910066491136390375">Peter Hedges is an American novelist, screenwriter, and film director. His novel <i>What's Eating Gilbert Grape</i> was adapted into a critically acclaimed movie of the same title, which launched his film career.<br/><br/>In 2002 he received an Academy Award nomination for Best Adapted Screenplay for <i>About a Boy</i>. In the same year, he wrote and directed <i>Pieces of April</i>, starring Katie Holmes, which he dedicated to </span>
  <span id="freeText8910066491136390375" style="display:none">Peter Hedges is an American novelist, screenwriter, and film director. His novel <i>What's Eating Gilbert Grape</i> was adapted into a critically acclaimed movie of the same title, which launched his film career.<br /><br />In 2002 he received an Academy Award nomination for Best Adapted Screenplay for <i>About a Boy</i>. In the same year, he wrote and directed <i>Pieces of April</i>, starring Katie Holmes, which he dedicated to his mother.<br /></span>
